    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_181416873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181416873" />
    <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks"><img alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577577052p2/3533262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181416873?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey (prettybooks)" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13416225-the-way-we-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-after-university">read-after-university</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181416873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11613536096450871399">Sixteen-year-old Kaelyn is living on a Canadian island when a viral epidemic occurs. People she’s known for her whole life start to get sick: <i>It starts with an itch you just can’t shake. Then comes a fever and a tickle in your throat. A few days later, you’ll be blabbing your secrets and chatting with strangers like they’re old friends. Three more, and the paranoid hallucinations kick in. And then you’re dead.</i><br/><br/>Kaelyn has faith in the government, believes that they’ll do everything they can to dis</span>
  <span id="freeText11613536096450871399" style="display:none">Sixteen-year-old Kaelyn is living on a Canadian island when a viral epidemic occurs. People she’s known for her whole life start to get sick: <i>It starts with an itch you just can’t shake. Then comes a fever and a tickle in your throat. A few days later, you’ll be blabbing your secrets and chatting with strangers like they’re old friends. Three more, and the paranoid hallucinations kick in. And then you’re dead.</i><br /><br />Kaelyn has faith in the government, believes that they’ll do everything they can to discover a cure for the virus, but then the island is quarantined—no one is allowed leave or enter. The community begins to feel abandoned. They must do everything they can to protect themselves, because no one else is going to.<br /><br />I enjoyed <i>The Way We Fall</i>, but I didn’t enjoy it as much as I wanted (and expected) to. It made me think about what I would do if an epidemic occurred in Britain. If a virus started spreading through England, Wales and Scotland, would they quarantine us and then leave to protect the rest of the world Would we have to fend for ourselves?<br /><br />However, I did have two main issues with the book. The first issue, and this is by no fault of the author or the book, is that I constantly felt like I reading something I’d already read before. I’ve read a few similar novels recently like <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/213753.Life_as_We_Knew_It__Last_Survivors___1_" title="Life as We Knew It (Last Survivors, #1) by Susan Beth Pfeffer" rel="nofollow noopener">Life as We Knew It</a>
</i>, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10841167.Dark_Inside__Dark_Inside___1_" title="Dark Inside (Dark Inside, #1) by Jeyn Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Inside</a>
</i>, and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9644151.Ashfall__Ashfall___1_" title="Ashfall (Ashfall, #1) by Mike Mullin" rel="nofollow noopener">Ashfall</a>
</i>, and so the events that occurred did not elicit any emotion in me. I wasn’t shocked by the way people behaved. I also suppose I <i>like</i> post-apocalyptic-type novels to be quite dramatic (i.e. zombies!) whereas <i>The Way We Fall</i> is much more understated and realistic. This is something I probably would have enjoyed more if I read it a year ago.<br /><br />The other, and most important, issue I had was with the narrative. The events are described to us through Kaelyn’s letters to her (ex-)best friend Leo. We know at the very start of the book that the two friends had an argument before Leo left the island to go to school. I felt that this was slightly forced and was only created as an excuse to have the narrative written the way it is. (However, this book <i>is</i> part of a series and it is hinted that Leo will have a role in the sequels.) The narrative didn’t really work for me because it meant that Kaelyn’s letters were brief, with only the bare minimum described. I thought that her voice came across as monotone and bland. I didn’t get to see real emotion, I think: the characters were odd in the sense that there’d be a death and everyone would just accept it and move on straight away. Because of this, I didn’t feel that the novel was as “poignant”, “powerful” or “gripping” as the <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UaFAuS5iqQY" rel="nofollow noopener">book trailer</a> and synopsis suggests. Nonetheless, this is just personal preference and I can see why others absolutely loved the novel and thought it was chilling and emotional.<br /><br /><i>This book was obtained as an e-Galley from Disney-Hyperion.</i><br /><br /><b>Dystopian or Not Dystopian?</b> Not Dystopian</span>
  <a data-text-id="11613536096450871399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_275846727" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/275846727" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/275846727?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=whiny-annoying-blah-heroine">whiny-annoying-blah-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer275846727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16378472177337193533"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>The Way We Fell is written in diary form from the perspective of a teenage girl called Kaelyn. Kaelyn lives on a remote island in Canada, she decides to write a journal for her childhood best friend and crush Leo, who she has not spoken to in 2 years. Leo has left the island to attend school in New York and Kaelyn plans to use the journal to straighten things out with him when he comes back from school.<br/>Kaelyn's entries start of that of a typical teenager, with her trying to make more an</span>
  <span id="freeText16378472177337193533" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />The Way We Fell is written in diary form from the perspective of a teenage girl called Kaelyn. Kaelyn lives on a remote island in Canada, she decides to write a journal for her childhood best friend and crush Leo, who she has not spoken to in 2 years. Leo has left the island to attend school in New York and Kaelyn plans to use the journal to straighten things out with him when he comes back from school.<br />Kaelyn's entries start of that of a typical teenager, with her trying to make more an effort to fit in at school and make friends. She regrets losing her friendship with Leo and not making it up to him before he left for school, so she promises to try harder with people.<br />When there is an outbreak of a deadly virus on the island, Kaelyn continues to write in her journal and records the hysteria that follows so when Leo comes back he will know what happened to Kaelyn, his family and his home. Kaelyn's account portray the bleakness and hopelessness of the situation very well; The Island is cut off from the mainland, supplies start running out, people start looting and hurting one another and the virus rampages through the island. <br />The narrative style took a while to get used to but once the story got going it added to the isolated tense situation of the island. Kaelyn was hard to relate to especially at first when she makes assumptions about her fellow classmates and judges those around her. She is quiet and can be awkward around people and she doesn't help herself or her goal to be more friendly and outgoing, thankfully as the story progresses Kaelyn comes out of her shell and connects with the people around her. Because everything is told in Kaelyn's perspective and what she assumes/thinks, everything has to be taken with a grain of salt as Kaelyn is not always a trustworthy narrater. <br />Kaelyn's relationship with her parents don't show her in a good light, she's childish, unreasonable and whiny around them but her relationship with her cousin and new friends Gav and Tessa bring out the best in Tessa. She is protective, kind and grateful for the new people in her life. Tessa is Leo's girlfriend and I was prepared to not like her for dating Kaelyn's crush but she was a brilliant character. She was a survivor and it was easy to see why Leo was with her, there were a few times when I wanted Tessa to be the narrater as I thought she was more interesting and relatable. <br />Kaelyn's relationship with Gav was cute and they suited each other quite well. It'll definitely be interesting to see the dynamics between Kaelyn, Gav and Leo when Leo makes an appearance in the next book. Kaelyn, Tessa and Gav are now connected through their experience with the virus so it'll be good to see how Leo will fit in with all the changes that have happened.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16378472177337193533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1623106982" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1623106982" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27646627-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447086953p2/27646627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1623106982?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/27646627-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1623106982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1928354170345428495">This just didn't work for me for a few reasons. I was intrigued by the premise (island community is plagued by a mysterious deadly virus and quarantined) and so expecting a lot more action and suspense then there actually was. There were points when I was just totally bored. It seemed like the plot was very repetitive--it's basically Kaeyln going back and forth between the hospital, her home, and various projects that she creates/signs up for to try to help. I also didn't buy the epistolary form</span>
  <span id="freeText1928354170345428495" style="display:none">This just didn't work for me for a few reasons. I was intrigued by the premise (island community is plagued by a mysterious deadly virus and quarantined) and so expecting a lot more action and suspense then there actually was. There were points when I was just totally bored. It seemed like the plot was very repetitive--it's basically Kaeyln going back and forth between the hospital, her home, and various projects that she creates/signs up for to try to help. I also didn't buy the epistolary format. The story is told through Kaelyn's letters to her estranged best friend, but the way they were written just seemed like a regular old novel from first-person point of view. I couldn't believe that it was truly her voice, which stopped me from connecting with her. In fact, I found her quite annoying, along with most of the other main teenage characters. They all seemed to have one defining, prodigious talent--Kaelyn with her knowledge of animal behavior, Tessa and her plants, Gav and his leadership, Warren and his organization/planning, Drew and his computer skills, Leo and his dancing. And then they were all just so noble, only wanting to help and protect each other. Really? You're not going to have even one iota of worry for your own safety, ever? I also got annoyed with Kaelyn's belief that she would be able to find a solution/cure by going through the medical records. Is she a prodigy at reading medical records, also? So much so that she would be able to determine a reason for the virus by looking at them when her father, a microbiologist couldn't? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ And then, of course, she does! Ugh. I at least was happy when her father said that he HAD thought of it, but that had ruled it out as too risky. Of course, all the clues to the possible cure for the virus were so OBVIOUS that I had put it together long before Kaelyn did, so maybe I'm a prodigy too.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Contributing to my boredom, I think, was the fact that I listened to the audiobook version. Kaelyn's letters were relatively short, and if I had read it myself I probably would have felt that it was paced much quicker (helped by the fact that I would skim through the boring parts). Listening to it, however, made me feel like she was just blathering on and on.<br /><br />There also wasn't much by way of ending. There's a kind-of climax, but then everything pretty much peters out in preparation for the next novel. I knew this was part of a series, but I expected SOME resolution. I kind of want to know what happens, but not enough to slog through Kaeyln's boring nobility. Maybe I'll just read a summary instead.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1928354170345428495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_271408047" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271408047" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3835702-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357322828p2/3835702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271408047?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/3835702-kat">Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=apocalypse">apocalypse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=udate">udate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3835702-kat?shelf=virus">virus</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271408047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5928957540518992400">Posted in full on: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://theaussiezombie.blogspot.com'>http://theaussiezombie.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/><b> 3 1/2 stars </b><br/><br/>Kaelyn and her family have recently moved back to “the island” where she grew up before moving to Toronto five years earlier. The story is told in first-person POV through Kaelyn’s eyes, in the form of journal entries to her friend Leo. The actual story behind Kaelyn and Leo’s relationship is revealed pretty gradually, most coming in the second half of the book. <br/><br/>The first 1/3 of the book moves quite slowly. Ms. Crewe works hard a</span>
  <span id="freeText5928957540518992400" style="display:none">Posted in full on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://theaussiezombie.blogspot.com">http://theaussiezombie.blogspot.com</a><br /><br /><b> 3 1/2 stars </b><br /><br />Kaelyn and her family have recently moved back to “the island” where she grew up before moving to Toronto five years earlier. The story is told in first-person POV through Kaelyn’s eyes, in the form of journal entries to her friend Leo. The actual story behind Kaelyn and Leo’s relationship is revealed pretty gradually, most coming in the second half of the book. <br /><br />The first 1/3 of the book moves quite slowly. Ms. Crewe works hard at building the character of Kaelyn and her attempts to re-integrate into her former friendships and explains her relationships with her parents, brother, uncle and niece. The disease also starts slowly, infecting a few people at a time and kept pretty much on the down-low by her father (who is also the chief doctor and an infectious diseases specialist at the island hospital). As the disease starts to spread, the government imposes quarantine and effectively leaves the island to its own devices. <br /><br />After reading through this first part of the book, I was firmly sitting on four stars – initially Kaelyn’s voice was a little immature and idealistic for a 16 year old, and I anticipated that the rest of the story would continue in those dumbed-down teenage niceties and all the important, loveable characters surviving to fight another day. <br /><br />And then I got to the 1/3 mark, and all of my opinions changed. Kaelyn developed into a more mature, emotional and involved character – and the story started to get gritty and dark. Without giving too much away (if I haven’t already, sorry!), there’s no happy ending to this story – characters that you fully expect to be alive and kickin’ well into the next book are suddenly no longer there (through a variety of causes), and Kaelyn is literally defending her life and the lives of those she loves. The origins and causes of the disease are further expanded upon and the story continues to get darker and darker, right up to the very last pages. <br /><br />The writing IS simplistic, but it fits perfectly with the pace and tone of the story – over-describing details would have stopped the heart-attack-edge-of-your-seat-I-may-just-cry tension and made the story far less believable. Although I understand journal-style books can be off-putting to some readers, it does fit perfectly with the book. <br /><br />In conclusion, I’ve struggled to rate this book. As I said earlier the first 1/3 was heading for a 4-star review, but the remaining 2/3 was solidly in 5-star territory and I’ll be looking forward to the next book in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5928957540518992400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_723369691" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/723369691" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/723369691?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-with-abbie">read-with-abbie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=as">as</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer723369691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6476561841590006012">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br/>16-year-old Kaelyn lives on an island off the shore of Canada. When a mysterious illness starts sweeping through the community, she assumes that her father who is a microbiologist will soon help the hospital staff to treat the virus; until people start dying from it.<br/>Suddenly the island is under quarantine, people are starting to act like vigilantes, and even more people are dying.<br/>What is this mysterious illness? Is there a cure? Can they find it in time? And h</span>
  <span id="freeText6476561841590006012" style="display:none">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br />16-year-old Kaelyn lives on an island off the shore of Canada. When a mysterious illness starts sweeping through the community, she assumes that her father who is a microbiologist will soon help the hospital staff to treat the virus; until people start dying from it.<br />Suddenly the island is under quarantine, people are starting to act like vigilantes, and even more people are dying.<br />What is this mysterious illness? Is there a cure? Can they find it in time? And how long will the quarantine last?<br /><br /><br />This was an interesting story, but I did find it a little odd in places.<br /><br />Kae was an okay character, but at times I felt like she lacked emotion. Several things that happened in this book were bad, really bad, and yet I didn’t feel like she was upset enough. If my close family members died the way hers did, I would be a basket case, yet she just seemed to take it all in her stride. She did show a little emotion when she found out that one of her friends had died, but it didn’t last long.<br /><br />The storyline in this was pretty good. I liked guessing who would get sick next, and watching out for little indicators as to who was about to go nuts. I wasn’t the biggest fan of the way the story was written – as Kae writing a letter/journal to her friend Leo who she hadn’t spoken to in 2 years, and I also thought that we weren’t really given much of an explanation as to why she hadn’t been speaking to him other than the fact that she was jealous!<br />The pace in this was quite leisurely, and at times I felt like there should have been a bit more excitement. People were dropping dead left, right, and centre, and yet the story didn’t really scare me at all. Maybe if we’d had some zombies it would have been a bit more interesting.<br /><br />The ending was okay, but it was a bit lack-lustre really. We didn’t get much of an explanation as to what had happened, where the virus had come from, or even how to treat it.<br />I will read the sequel, because I’ve already got a copy, but I’m not really sure where the story is going to go from here.<br />Overall; an okay story about a new and deadly virus, but lacking emotion and explanation.<br />6.75 out of 10.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6476561841590006012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1338010927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1338010927" />
    <a title="Cesar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34467577-cesar"><img alt="Cesar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501005350p2/34467577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1338010927?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cesar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cesar" href="/user/show/34467577-cesar">Cesar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1338010927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15754648864339509093">4.5 star <br/><br/><i>
  <b>“Most people think the scariest thing is knowing that you’re going to die. It’s not. It’s knowing you might have to watch every single person you’ve ever loved – or even liked – waste away while you just stand there.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Which is worse: something deadly you can see, or an invisible killer. If you chose the latter, then get ready for one scary ride.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>The Way We Fall</b>
</i> is by no means a scary book. It's not one of those books where you sleep with the lights on, checking to make sure you ha</span>
  <span id="freeText15754648864339509093" style="display:none">4.5 star <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Most people think the scariest thing is knowing that you’re going to die. It’s not. It’s knowing you might have to watch every single person you’ve ever loved – or even liked – waste away while you just stand there.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Which is worse: something deadly you can see, or an invisible killer. If you chose the latter, then get ready for one scary ride.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>The Way We Fall</b>
</i> is by no means a scary book. It's not one of those books where you sleep with the lights on, checking to make sure you have a weapon by your bedside table. It's scary in the sense that something like a deadly epidemic could happen. And as we know throughout history, it had. The Black Plague, the Spanish Influenza, and many others that have killed hundreds of thousands of people. And it could happen soon. That alone is what makes this book scary.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“Our virus is a lot smarter than the ones you see in zombie movies. It doesn't make its victims stagger around slobbering and moaning so anyone in their right minds would run the other way. It gets you cozying up to people so you cough and sneeze it right into their faces. <br />We just need the vaccine. Then we'll be okay.”</b>
</i><br /><br />I am a huge fan of anything apocalyptic. Virus outbreak, nuclear holocaust, natural disasters that cause massive damage. Those are my type of books. <br /><br />Through out reading this, I was legit worried for Kaelyn and the other people. This book is no walk in the park. People die. Young and old. And it's not pretty.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“This is what we do. We make tea and read books and watch people die.”</b>
</i><br /><br />One thing I liked was how it all took place on an island. Just imagine an island of people cut off from the outside world. People trying to survive on the limited resources. Chaos is bound to happen. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“You learn a lot when you know no one else is going to do things for you.”</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>The Way We Fall</b>
</i> shows first hand of humanity slowly slipping away. It was scary but so damn good. I would definitely recommend this one!<br /><br />Thanks for reading my review!<br /><br />-Cesar</span>
  <a data-text-id="15754648864339509093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_182193981" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182193981" />
    <a title="Elizabeth B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2940273-elizabeth-b"><img alt="Elizabeth B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1273006772p2/2940273.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182193981?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth B" href="/user/show/2940273-elizabeth-b">Elizabeth B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182193981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer303227647382642474">While the premise is a good one, I had a LOT of problems with this book. Supposedly, it is a collection of letters written to her former best friend Leo but except for the date entries, very few are in letter format and, instead, are written in novel type prose. This bothered me more than it should have I suppose but it drove me crazy that we were to believe these letters that were fully formed dialogue (with tags no less!) were simple notes written to a friend. Why not pick one or the other sty</span>
  <span id="freeText303227647382642474" style="display:none">While the premise is a good one, I had a LOT of problems with this book. Supposedly, it is a collection of letters written to her former best friend Leo but except for the date entries, very few are in letter format and, instead, are written in novel type prose. This bothered me more than it should have I suppose but it drove me crazy that we were to believe these letters that were fully formed dialogue (with tags no less!) were simple notes written to a friend. Why not pick one or the other style to write in? Either write it as letters or write it as prose…combining the two made for just a completely unbelievable premise. If the reader can’t believe the letter is truthful then why should we believe any of the events that occur are truthful? It just gnawed at me through the entire book. <br /><br />The plot itself was a promising one but it moved ever so slowly and you got no sense of emotion from the main character. She didn’t write to her friend of her fears of what was going on around her just a journalistic reporting of events which made it hard to care about her. There was no emotional ramble about how she feared for the safety of her family and friends and, even after some of her classmates perish, there is still no emotional response from her.<br /><br />I really wanted to like this book because it sounded similar to many of the yellow fever books I’ve read over the last few years but unfortunately, it just did not live up to my expectations.<br /><br />(ARC Galley Proof)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="303227647382642474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_204895974" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/204895974" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/327471-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1188525077p2/327471.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204895974?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/327471-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/327471-kristen?shelf=romance-y">romance-y</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/327471-kristen?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/327471-kristen?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204895974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18338315641435855488">First Impression:<br/>I enjoyed Megan Crewe's first book and was excited to see that this one tackled a virus going out of control on an island.<br/><br/>While Reading:<br/>The voice of Kaelyn rings out strong straight from the beginning. She's missing her best friend, whom she didn't have a chance to mend their friendship before he left the island. Kaelyn is now back to stay on the island for a while. The Way We Fall is written as a journal from Kaelyn to Leo, her best friend and maybe something more if she had fi</span>
  <span id="freeText18338315641435855488" style="display:none">First Impression:<br />I enjoyed Megan Crewe's first book and was excited to see that this one tackled a virus going out of control on an island.<br /><br />While Reading:<br />The voice of Kaelyn rings out strong straight from the beginning. She's missing her best friend, whom she didn't have a chance to mend their friendship before he left the island. Kaelyn is now back to stay on the island for a while. The Way We Fall is written as a journal from Kaelyn to Leo, her best friend and maybe something more if she had fixed things between them.<br /><br />When the virus starts to break free, it starts with her friend's father, and spirals to those she loves and knows. The government puts the island under quarantine, but eventually abandons them and small bursts of chaos ensue. People cannot leave the island or they may be shot. Food packages and medicine stop being delivered. It's the type of story that happens before an apocalypse and it definitely has you thinking - this could really happen.<br /><br />Crewe paints a realistic world where something like this could happen. A disease that kills and kills and progresses in a way to spread more quickly. There's some romance and relationship building to lead you into what seems will be a compelling series that will keep you reading onto the next book.<br /><br />Final Verdict:<br />Definitely a series I will be reading on. I've become quite attached to the characters left and would like to meet this Leo that Kaelyn can't seem to give up on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18338315641435855488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_186599091" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186599091" />
    <a title="Charlotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5284833-charlotte"><img alt="Charlotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592712966p2/5284833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186599091?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte" href="/user/show/5284833-charlotte">Charlotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5284833-charlotte?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5284833-charlotte?shelf=2012-challenge">2012-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5284833-charlotte?shelf=re-reading">re-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5284833-charlotte?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5284833-charlotte?shelf=2011-challenge">2011-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5284833-charlotte?shelf=january-2012">january-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5284833-charlotte?shelf=january-2012-releases">january-2012-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186599091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6766879045034213120">I absolutely loved the way this book was written. The journal style gave us one person's (Kaelyn) perspective of the events, while tying them in with the emotional situation she is going through with the person she is writing to (Leo, her former best friend).<br/><br/>I thought this was a cleverly written story. The accounts Kaelyn gives of the sequence of events that occur as a virus begins killing off people on the island where she lives, are real and terrifying. She describes them in startling detail a</span>
  <span id="freeText6766879045034213120" style="display:none">I absolutely loved the way this book was written. The journal style gave us one person's (Kaelyn) perspective of the events, while tying them in with the emotional situation she is going through with the person she is writing to (Leo, her former best friend).<br /><br />I thought this was a cleverly written story. The accounts Kaelyn gives of the sequence of events that occur as a virus begins killing off people on the island where she lives, are real and terrifying. She describes them in startling detail and realistic emotion, all while managing to form great character development for herself as well as pretty much everyone she encounters. You really feel like she is telling you the story of what's happening there. <br /><br />There are so many tragic turns and twists to this story that I had a hard time putting it down. You are on the edge of your seat wondering who will get the symptoms, who will be next!<br /><br />The ending of the book was a bit abrupt for my taste, but after I thought about it, I have come to realize it really could not have been told any other way.<br /><br />I highly recommend this book!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6766879045034213120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zT/Wx3t1TyrsAdRkS8CkyKBHXiHqqFJ5V8HX1zZ5QKj//4j4JvgTAPkruamWy5O72FmX7/jwmrxsj5DWhDGQgA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dbjRCQ7vSLdz4vO+oKisdUru+SpgF9Jf3ovhaBW0juZHeI82U2IUnWbInnN9o5sGMvAw5HJPGprlxaZpp/xezg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8401234861272507222">Like many authors, Megan Crewe finds writing about herself much more difficult than making things up. A few definite facts: she lives in Toronto, Canada with her husband and son (and does on occasion say "eh"), she tutors children and teens with special needs, and she's spent the last six years studying kung fu, so you should probably be nice to her. She has been making up stories about magic and </span>
  <span id="freeText8401234861272507222" style="display:none">Like many authors, Megan Crewe finds writing about herself much more difficult than making things up. A few definite facts: she lives in Toronto, Canada with her husband and son (and does on occasion say "eh"), she tutors children and teens with special needs, and she's spent the last six years studying kung fu, so you should probably be nice to her. She has been making up stories about magic and spirits and other what ifs since before she knew how to write words on paper. These days the stories are just a lot longer. <br /><br />Megan's first novel, GIVE UP THE GHOST, was shortlisted for the Sunburst Award for Canadian Literature of the Fantastic. Her second, THE WAY WE FALL, was nominated for the White Pine Award and made the International Reading Association Young Adults' Choices List. Her Fallen World trilogy (THE WAY WE FALL, THE LIVES WE LOST, THE WORLDS WE MAKE) is now complete and she has a new trilogy forthcoming in October 2014, beginning with EARTH &amp; SKY. Her books have been published in translation in several countries around the world. She has also published short stories in magazines such as On Spec and Brutarian Quarterly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8401234861272507222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
